8. Duplicate Strings:  overhead 67.4%  ( 682,486Kb )  What's this?

  Total strings   Unique strings   Duplicate values  Overhead 
 13,717,134 79,858 57,078682,486Kb (67.4%)

What can I do to fix Duplicate Strings?


The overhead (waste) of all 13,717,134 duplicate strings is 682,486Kb, or 67.4% of used heap.
That's how much memory you could save if all your string values were unique,
i.e. all problematic strings were de-duplicated, for example using the String.intern() call.

Duplicate strings wasting 440,797Kb, or 43.5% of used heap are referenced directly by JDK classes.
  j.u.LinkedList$Node.item (8,501,545 strings, waste 440,797Kb, or 43.5% of used heap)

How to fix?

Such strings may be hard to de-duplicate.
You may need to use reflection to intern strings managed by some JDK classes.
Check this article for more information



Duplicate strings wasting 238,038Kb, or 23.5% of used heap are referenced by collections or arrays in JDK classes.
  String[] (5,121,148 strings, waste 238,038Kb, or 23.5% of used heap)
    ↖j.u.StringJoiner.elts

How to fix?

Such strings may be hard to de-duplicate.
You will need to check the code of the respective JDK classes to understand how they
initialize and manage the strings in internal collections.
Depending on how these internals work, you may be able to pass deduplicated strings
to these classes, or use reflection to deduplicate these strings in place.
Check this article for more information



For detailed information about duplicate strings in this dump, check the tables below.
To learn more about fixing duplicate strings, check this article
